msg:It is ~5km away from the main tourist spots (old town, mosque etc). While it may have been the best hotel in the past, it now feels a bit old. The rooms are ok, beds are comfortable but AC didn't work and it was 28C in the room! the windows didn't close properly (we had a huge sandstorm and the air was really bad). They have a swimming pool in the basement but it was being repaired when we went. Pool opening hours are funny (3-10pm) while a morning swim would be nice. The staff is friendly and tries its best to help out. they have a mini market with drinks and fruits etc, which is convenient. they are supposed to have a sightseeing teahouse on the top floor (37th) but the whole floor was completely destroyed and abandoned, very strange.
Breakfast is ok, nothing special. On a clear day, the view looking south is amazing (on Kongur Shan at 7600 m high).

msg:The best hotel I stayed in during my trip to southern Xinjiang!
When I booked, I saw that it was a five-star hotel on Ctrip. Everyone knows that five-star does not equal five-star. I didn't expect that it was a formal five-star hotel.
It looks like an old five-star hotel. It has everything it should have. The room is the same as the promotional pictures. The key is that the service is very, very good.
From the front desk to the room service, everything is very good. This is the first time I have encountered a hotel room that is cleaned several times a day! It was cleaned at noon, went out for a meal in the afternoon, and was cleaned again when I came back in the evening.
The hotel's breakfast variety is not much, but southerners come to Xinjiang lack vegetables. The five kinds of stir-fried vegetables every day are great. There are also freshly baked naan and handmade ramen.
